      <p>The <b>Republic of Singapore</b> is an <a href="/wiki/Island" title="Island">island</a> <a href="/wiki/Country" title="Country">country</a> and a <a href="/wiki/City-state" title="City-state">city-state</a>. It is at the southern end of the <a href="/wiki/Malay_Peninsula" title="Malay Peninsula">Malay Peninsula</a> in <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>. Singapore is about one degree of latitude (137 kilometres or 85 miles) north of the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">equator</a>. Its closest neighbors are <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>. About 5.40 million <a href="https://simple.wiktionary.org/wiki/people" class="extiw" title="wikt:people">people</a> live in Singapore. About 3.31 million are <a href="/wiki/Citizenship" title="Citizenship">citizens</a>. Most of them (76%) are <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">ethnically</a> <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a>, an old <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">Indian</a> language, "Singaporean", from which Singapore got its name, means "<a href="/wiki/Lion" title="Lion">Lion</a> City" commonly ruled by <a href="/wiki/Sultan" title="Sultan">Sultans</a>. </p>
      <p>Singapore is also commonly known as a "Garden City" or a "City in a Garden". It is because there are plants everywhere, making it look like a garden.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[8]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>It is also sometimes jokingly called a "fine" city. Not only does the city have a very high <a href="/wiki/Standard_of_living" title="Standard of living">standard of living</a>, but it is also known for having many strict rules and <a href="/wiki/Punishment" title="Punishment">punishments</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Fine" title="Fine">fines</a>. </p>
      <p>The national <a href="/wiki/Language" title="***REMOVED***">language</a> of Singapore is <a href="/wiki/Malay_language" title="Malay language">Malay</a>. Other <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a>s of Singapore are <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Mandarin language">Mandarin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">Tamil</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-statutes.agc.gov.sg_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statutes.agc.gov.sg-11">[9]</a></sup> English is the language of choice because it is the language that almost everyone in Singapore knows. It is the first language taught in schools and the language used by the <a href="/wiki/Government" title="Government">government</a>. <a href="/wiki/Student" title="Student">Students</a> are also taught their first language. This means that the Chinese will learn Mandarin, Malays will learn Malay, and so on. Students can also choose to learn a third language in <a href="/wiki/Secondary_school" title="Secondary school">secondary school</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MOE-LP_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MOE-LP-12">[10]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=1" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: History">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Change section: History">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="floatright">
       <a href="/wiki/File:StamfordRaffles.jpeg" class="image" title="Picture of Sir Stamford Raffles"><img alt="Picture of Sir Stamford Raffles" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/StamfordRaffles.jpeg/200px-StamfordRaffles.jpeg" decoding="async" width="200" height="307" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/StamfordRaffles.jpeg/300px-StamfordRaffles.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/StamfordRaffles.jpeg/400px-StamfordRaffles.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="1536"></a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Before_1819">Before 1819</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=2" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Before 1819">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Change section: Before 1819">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Singapore's name comes from 'Singa Pura', which means Lion City in <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a>. According to the Sejarah Melayu (Malay Annals), a <a href="/wiki/Sumatra" title="Sumatra">Sumatran</a> prince called Sang Nila Utama landed on Temasek<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[11]</a></sup> (Singapore's old name) and saw a <a href="/wiki/Lion" title="Lion">Lion</a> which is called 'Singa' in Malay. Thus he gave the <a href="/wiki/Island" title="Island">island</a> a new name, 'Singapura'.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[12]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>However, Sang Nila Utama, the real founder of Singapore in the 13th century, (although there is some debates about Raffles and Farquhar who founded Singapore which is found to be false) was likely mistaken, as lions never existed in Singapore. It is believed that the "lion" was actually a <a href="/wiki/Malayan_Tiger" class="mw-redirect" title="Malayan Tiger">Malayan Tiger</a>, which exists in neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, and is <a href="/wiki/Extinct" class="mw-redirect" title="Extinct">extinct</a> in Singapore. There were also many pieces of old items, such as Chinese coins, that showed that Temasek was a trading port even before the British rule.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Straits_Times_2016_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Straits_Times_2016-15">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[14]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1819_to_1940">1819 to 1940</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=3" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: 1819 to 1940">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Change section: 1819 to 1940">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Few people lived in Singapore at the beginning of the 19th century. <a href="/wiki/Stamford_Raffles" title="Stamford Raffles">Sir Thomas Stamford Raffles</a> set up a <a href="/wiki/Britain" class="mw-redirect" title="Britain">British</a> <a href="/wiki/Trade" title="Trade">trading</a> town in <a href="/wiki/1819" title="1819">1819</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[15]</a></sup> and it became an important town in the Malay Archipelago, "Singapore". The country was given <a href="/wiki/Colony" title="Colony">colony</a> rank in <a href="/wiki/1867" title="1867">1867</a>. </p>
      <p>When Raffles landed in Singapore, he paid the then <a href="/wiki/Sultan" title="Sultan">Sultan</a> a sum of money for a piece of land in the South of Singapore. In August 1824, Dr. John Crawfurd signed a treaty with the Sultan for control over the whole tropical island. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II">World War II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=4" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: World War II">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Change section: World War II">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:JapaneseMarchSgpCity.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/JapaneseMarchSgpCity.jpg/200px-JapaneseMarchSgpCity.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/JapaneseMarchSgpCity.jpg/300px-JapaneseMarchSgpCity.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/JapaneseMarchSgpCity.jpg/400px-JapaneseMarchSgpCity.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1598" data-file-height="1053"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:JapaneseMarchSgpCity.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Japanese marching in Singapore during the World War II period
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Occupation_of_Singapore" title="Japanese Occupation of Singapore">Japanese Occupation of Singapore</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Due to the weak <a href="/wiki/Defense_(military)" title="Defense (military)">defenses</a> of the country, the Japanese attacked Singapore and took control of the colony on <a href="/wiki/15_February" class="mw-redirect" title="15 February">15 February</a> <a href="/wiki/1942" title="1942">1942</a>. People of Singapore went through hard times during the Japanese rule, until the surrender of the Japanese in September <a href="/wiki/1945" title="1945">1945</a>. This was called the Japanese occupation. Singapore was then returned to the British. </p>
      <p>Many people were <a href="/wiki/Torture" title="Torture">tortured</a> or killed by the Japanese as they did not follow the rules properly or because they were suspected of going against the Japanese. The most notable anti-Japanese force was <a href="/w/index.php?title=Force_136&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Force 136 (not yet started)">Force 136</a>, headed by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lim_Bo_Seng&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Lim Bo Seng (not yet started)">Lim Bo Seng</a>. Its purpose was to encourage and supply resistance movements in the enemy-occupied territory and occasionally mount clandestine sabotage operations. </p>
      <p>The hard times during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> made the people think that the British were not as strong as before. Therefore, many people wanted <a href="/wiki/Independence" title="Independence">independence</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[16]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence">Independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=5" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Independence">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Change section: Independence">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/1963" title="1963">1963</a> Singapore joined with <a href="/wiki/British_Malaya" title="British Malaya">Malaya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sabah" title="Sabah">Sabah</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sarawak" title="Sarawak">Sarawak</a> to form the new nation of <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>. Malaysia is a country with many <a href="/wiki/Race_(sociology)" title="Race (sociology)">races</a>. In Malaya, only the <a href="/wiki/Malays" title="Malays">Malays</a> have special benefits. For example, the Malays can get university education more easily than other races. </p>
      <p>As most people in Singapore are <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>, Singapore wanted <a href="/wiki/Social_equality" title="Social equality">equality</a> for all the people of Malaysia. Singapore also wanted a common market to be set up so that goods to Malaysia would not be taxed. However, this was not done and caused arguments between the <a href="/wiki/State" title="State">state</a> <a href="/wiki/Government" title="Government">government</a> of Singapore and the <a href="/wiki/Federal_republic" title="Federal republic">federal</a> government of Malaysia. </p>
      <p>Singapore separated from Malaysia and became <a href="/wiki/Independent" class="mw-redirect" title="Independent">independent</a> on its own on <a href="/wiki/9_August" class="mw-redirect" title="9 August">9 August</a> <a href="/wiki/1965" title="1965">1965</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[17]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="After_Independence">After Independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=6" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: After Independence">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Change section: After Independence">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>After Independence, the president of Singapore was <a href="/w/index.php?title=Yusof_bin_Ishak&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Yusof bin Ishak (not yet started)">Yusof bin Ishak</a> and its prime minister was <a href="/wiki/Lee_Kuan_Yew" title="Lee Kuan Yew">Lee Kuan Yew</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[18]</a></sup> At first, many people thought Singapore would not be able to continue on its own. In 1967 Singapore helped to start the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Southeast_Asian_Nations" title="Association of Southeast Asian Nations">Association of Southeast Asian Nations</a><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[19]</a></sup> and in 1970 it joined the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a>. Lee Kuan Yew was in charge of the country as <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Singapore" title="Prime Minister of Singapore">Prime Minister of Singapore</a> and saw it become very <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[22]</a></sup> In 1990, <a href="/wiki/Goh_Chok_Tong" title="Goh Chok Tong">Goh Chok Tong</a> replaced Lee Kuan Yew as prime minister, while Lee Kuan Yew became <a href="/wiki/Senior_Minister" title="Senior Minister">Senior Minister</a>. When Goh Chok Tong was Prime Minister, Singapore went through the <a href="/w/index.php?title=1997_Asian_Financial_Crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="1997 Asian Financial Crisis (not yet started)">1997 Asian Financial Crisis</a>, the 2003 <a href="/wiki/SARS" class="mw-redirect" title="SARS">SARS</a> outbreak and <a href="/wiki/Terrorist" class="mw-redirect" title="Terrorist">terrorist</a> threats by <a href="/wiki/Jemaah_Islamiyah" title="Jemaah Islamiyah">Jemaah Islamiyah</a>. In 2004, <a href="/wiki/Lee_Hsien_Loong" title="Lee Hsien Loong">Lee Hsien Loong</a>, the son of Lee Kuan Yew, took over as Prime Minister. Goh Chok Tong became the Senior Minister, and Lee Kuan Yew became the <a href="/wiki/Minister_Mentor" title="Minister Mentor">Minister Mentor</a> of Singapore. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=7" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Government and politics">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Change section: Government and politics">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Parliament_House_Singapore.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Parliament_House_Singapore.jpg/250px-Parliament_House_Singapore.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Parliament_House_Singapore.jpg/375px-Parliament_House_Singapore.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Parliament_House_Singapore.jpg/500px-Parliament_House_Singapore.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Parliament_House_Singapore.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Singapore's <a href="/w/index.php?title=Parliament_House,_Singapore&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Parliament House, Singapore (not yet started)">Parliament House</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Singapore is a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_republic" title="Parliamentary republic">parliamentary republic</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Westminster_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Westminster system">Westminster system</a> of <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">unicameral</a> parliamentary government representing <a href="/wiki/Constituency" title="Constituency">constituencies</a>. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Constitution_of_Singapore&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Constitution of Singapore (not yet started)">Its constitution</a> states <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" class="mw-redirect" title="Representative democracy">representative democracy</a> as its political system.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-25">[23]</a></sup> In 2011 <a href="/w/index.php?title=Freedom_House&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Freedom House (not yet started)">Freedom House</a> ranked Singapore as "partly free" in its <i>Freedom in the World</i> report,<sup id="cite_ref-freedomhouse_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freedomhouse-26">[24]</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i> ranked Singapore as a "hybrid regime", the third rank out of four, in its "Democracy Index".<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[25]</a></sup> Singapore is ranked regularly as one of the least <a href="/wiki/Corruption" title="Corruption">corrupt</a> countries in the world, according to <a href="/w/index.php?title=Transparency_International&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Transparency International (not yet started)">Transparency International</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[26]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cabinet_of_Singapore&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Cabinet of Singapore (not yet started)">Cabinet</a> has <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive power</a>, and is led by the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Singapore" title="Prime Minister of Singapore">Prime Minister</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Singapore" title="President of Singapore">President</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Law_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law-29">[27]</a></sup> The president is elected through <a href="/wiki/Suffrage" title="Suffrage">popular vote</a>, and has some <a href="/wiki/Veto" title="Veto">veto powers</a> for a few big decisions such as the use of the national reserves and the appointment of judges, but otherwise occupies a post with little power.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[28]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Parliament_of_Singapore&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Parliament of Singapore (not yet started)">Parliament</a> serves as the <a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">legislative branch</a> of government.<sup id="cite_ref-Law_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law-29">[27]</a></sup> Members of Parliament (MPs) are made up of elected, non-constituency and nominated members. Elected MPs are voted into parliament on a "<a href="/wiki/First-past-the-post_voting" title="First-past-the-post voting">first-past-the-post</a>" (plurality) system and represent either single-member or group-representation constituencies.<sup id="cite_ref-parliament.gov.sg_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-parliament.gov.sg-31">[29]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Action_Party" title="People's Action Party">People's Action Party</a> has won control of Parliament with large majorities in every election since self-governance in 1959.<sup id="cite_ref-freedomhouse_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freedomhouse-26">[24]</a></sup> However, in the most recent parliamentary elections in 2011, the opposition, led by the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Workers%27_Party_of_Singapore&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Workers' Party of Singapore (not yet started)">Workers' Party</a>, made large and important gains and increased its representation in the House to 6 elected MPs, and two nominated MPs.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[30]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The legal system of Singapore is based on <a href="/w/index.php?title=English_common_law&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="English common law (not yet started)">English common law</a>, however with large and important local differences. <a href="/wiki/Trial_by_jury" class="mw-redirect" title="Trial by jury">Trial by jury</a> was completely removed in 1970 leaving <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">judicial</a> judgement done completely and only by <a href="/wiki/Judge" title="Judge">judgeship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[31]</a></sup> Singapore has punishments that include <a href="/w/index.php?title=Judicial_corporal_punishment&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Judicial corporal punishment (not yet started)">judicial corporal punishment</a> in the form of caning for <a href="/wiki/Rape" title="Rape">rape</a>, <a href="/wiki/Riot" title="Riot">rioting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vandalism" title="Vandalism">vandalism</a>, and some immigration crimes.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[33]</a></sup> There is a mandatory <a href="/wiki/Death_penalty" title="Death penalty">death penalty</a> for <a href="/wiki/Murder" title="Murder">murder</a>, and for certain <a href="/wiki/Illegal_drug_trade" title="Illegal drug trade">drug-trafficking</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gun" title="Gun">firearms</a> offences.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[34]</a></sup> In a 2008 survey, international business executives believed Singapore, together with Hong Kong, had the best judicial system in Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[35]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="People">People</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=8" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: People">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Change section: People">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=9" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Religion">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Change section: Religion">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> is the most common religion in Singapore.<sup id="cite_ref-census2010_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census2010-38">[36]</a></sup> Other common religions include: <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taoism" title="Taoism">Taoism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-census2010_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census2010-38">[36]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=10" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Education">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Change section: Education">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;">

          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Degree</td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:green; width:13%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">13%</td> 
          </tr> 
         </tbody>
        </table> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <p>Students in Singapore go through six years of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Compulsory_education&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Compulsory education (not yet started)">compulsory</a><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[38]</a></sup> Primary school, which ends with all students taking a Primary School Leaving Examination (<a href="/w/index.php?title=PSLE&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="PSLE (not yet started)">PSLE</a>). Then, depending on their results in the PSLE, students are <a href="/wiki/Streaming_(education)" class="mw-redirect" title="Streaming (education)">streamed</a> into "Special", "Express", "Normal (Academic)", and "Normal (Technical)" groups.<sup id="cite_ref-Sec-Sch_Courses_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sec-Sch_Courses-41">[39]</a></sup> The amount of time a student spends studying in Secondary school (4–5 years) depends on their group.<sup id="cite_ref-Sec-Sch_Courses_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sec-Sch_Courses-41">[39]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Students are taught in English and their mother tongue, which can be <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malay_language" title="Malay language">Malay</a> or <a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">Tamil</a>. Secondary school students may also choose to study a third language such as:<sup id="cite_ref-MOE-LP_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MOE-LP-12">[10]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">Japanese</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Malay_language" title="Malay language">Malay</a> special programme – For non-Malay speakers</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a> special programme – For non-Chinese speakers</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Students can take a third language as it increases their chances in getting an overseas <a href="/wiki/Scholarship" title="Scholarship">scholarship</a> and can improve their examination grades, especially in the <a href="/w/index.php?title=GCE_Ordinary_Level&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="GCE Ordinary Level (not yet started)">GCE Ordinary Level</a> ("O" Levels), which are Secondary students take after their five or four years of education.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[40]</a></sup> However, only some students can qualify to take a third language.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[41]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After their "O" Levels, students can choose to go to a <a href="/w/index.php?title=Polytechnic&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Polytechnic (not yet started)">polytechnic</a>, which is a place where students can study for 3 years for a <a href="/wiki/Diploma" title="Diploma">diploma</a><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[42]</a></sup> or to a <a href="/wiki/Junior_college" class="mw-redirect" title="Junior college">junior college</a> where students study for 2 years to receive an <a href="/wiki/GCE_Advanced_Level" title="GCE Advanced Level">"A" Level</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[43]</a></sup> Students can also go to Institutes of Technical Education (ITE), where students study for two years to receive a "National ITE Certificate" (NITEC). This certificate is only recognized in Singapore. Students who go to ITE usually continue their education at a polytechnic. </p>
      <p>With either a diploma, or an "A" Level <a href="/wiki/Certificate" title="Certificate">certificate</a>, students can apply to go to <a href="/wiki/Universities" class="mw-redirect" title="Universities">universities</a> in Singapore or overseas.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[44]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=11" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Languages">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Change section: Languages">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;"> 
       <div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;"> 
        <table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;"> 
         <tbody>
          <tr style="background:#ddd">
           <th style="text-align:center;" colspan="5">Language used most frequently at home<sup id="cite_ref-singstat1_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-singstat1-47">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[46]</a></sup></th>
          </tr> 
          <tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;"> 
           <td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:left;">Language</td> 
           <td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:right;"></td> 
           <td style="width:100px; text-align:left;"></td> 
           <td style="padding:0 4px; width:1em; text-align:right;">Percent</td> 
           <td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:right;"></td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">English</td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:blue; width:36.9%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">36.9%</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Mandarin</td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:yellow; width:34.9%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">34.9%</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Malay</td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:red; width:10.7%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">10.7%</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Tamil</td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:green; width:3.3%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">3.3%</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Others</td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:grey; width:14.2%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">14.2%</td> 
          </tr> 
         </tbody>
        </table> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Government_of_Singapore&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Government of Singapore (not yet started)">Singapore government</a> has chosen four official languages: <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malay_language" title="Malay language">Malay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_Chinese" title="Mandarin Chinese">Chinese (Mandarin)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">Tamil</a>. English is the primary language.<sup id="cite_ref-statutes.agc.gov.sg_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statutes.agc.gov.sg-11">[9]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Singapore_English" class="mw-redirect" title="Singapore English">Singapore English</a> is the main language in Singapore.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[47]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>English is the first language of the nation, but it is not the most common. English is the second most commonly spoken language among Singaporeans. The most commonly spoken language amongst Singaporeans in their homes is Chinese (51%), followed by English (32%), Malay (13%) and Tamil (7%). This means that 32% of Singaporeans are native English speakers. Most of the rest of the people speak it as a second language. However, English has the largest total number of speakers including native and second language speakers. <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_Chinese" title="Mandarin Chinese">Mandarin Chinese</a> is the second most common.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-50">[48]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-51">[49]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Almost 40% of people in Singapore are foreign.<sup id="cite_ref-un.org_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-un.org-52">[50]</a></sup> Most foreigners come from Asia. The two countries where most foreigners come from are <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> (mostly <a href="/w/index.php?title=Malaysian_Chinese&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Malaysian Chinese (not yet started)">Malaysian Chinese</a>) and <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>. In 2009, there may have been 350,000 Malaysians working in Singapore.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[51]</a></sup> Many Chinese-speaking foreigners and Chinese-speaking Singaporeans work in services. Thus, Chinese is the main language of many workers such as hawkers, retail assistants, <a href="/wiki/Hairdresser" title="Hairdresser">hairdressers</a>, etc. in Singapore today.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[53]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Singapore_from_Chinatown.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Singapore_from_Chinatown.jpg/200px-Singapore_from_Chinatown.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Singapore_from_Chinatown.jpg/300px-Singapore_from_Chinatown.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Singapore_from_Chinatown.jpg/400px-Singapore_from_Chinatown.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Singapore_from_Chinatown.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Singapore from <a href="/wiki/Chinatown,_Singapore" title="Chinatown, Singapore">Chinatown</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Singapore_English" class="mw-redirect" title="Singapore English">Singaporean English</a> mainly comes from <a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">British English</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[54]</a></sup> The forms of English spoken in Singapore range from <a href="/wiki/Standard_English" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard English">Standard English</a> to a <a href="/wiki/Pidgin" title="Pidgin">pidgin</a> called <a href="/wiki/Singlish" title="Singlish">Singlish</a>. The Singapore government and many Singaporeans are against using <a href="/wiki/Singlish" title="Singlish">Singlish</a>. There is a "Speak Good English" campaign each year. <a href="/wiki/Public_school" title="Public school">Public schools</a> and in the media also have rules against Singlish.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[55]</a></sup> There are many Singapore accents in English because of the many languages and identities of people in the city. Languages can even change over the generations and children may speak different languages and have different accents from their mother. For example, in a Singaporean Chinese family, the grandmother might speak <a href="/wiki/Hokkien" title="Hokkien">Hokkien</a> as her first language. Differently, the mother might speak Mandarin as her first language and Hokkien/English as her second languages, while the grandson might speak English as his first language and Mandarin as his second language. </p>
      <p>Before independence in 1965, <a href="/wiki/Hokkien" title="Hokkien">Hokkien</a>, a Chinese dialect, was the common language among the Chinese laborers. Malay and English were used to communicate between the different ethnic groups.<sup id="cite_ref-country-data.com_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-country-data.com-58">[56]</a></sup> After independence in 1965, English became the first language of the nation and replaced Hokkien and Malay as the one shared language. Today, most younger Singaporeans have English as their first language or are fluent in English. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Malay_language" title="Malay language">Malay</a> is a national language of Singapore because of the history of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-statutes.agc.gov.sg_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statutes.agc.gov.sg-11">[9]</a></sup> However, less than 20% of Singaporeans can read and write in Malay. Malay is still used at home by most <a href="/w/index.php?title=Malays_in_Singapore&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Malays in Singapore (not yet started)">Singaporean Malays</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Afendras1980_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Afendras1980-59">[57]</a></sup> The Malay used in Singapore (Bahasa Melayu) is closer to the language in Malaysia than the language in Indonesia. However, there are differences between the Malay in Singapore and in Malaysia. The national anthem "<a href="/wiki/Majulah_Singapura" title="Majulah Singapura">Majulah Singapura</a>" is sung in Malay. </p>
      <p>Many people speak Chinese – <a href="/w/index.php?title=Singaporean_Mandarin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Singaporean Mandarin (not yet started)">Mandarin</a> and other Chinese <a href="/wiki/Dialect" title="Dialect">dialects</a> – in Singapore. Just over 50% of Singaporeans speak it at home, so it is the most common language in homes.<sup id="cite_ref-Afendras1980_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Afendras1980-59">[57]</a></sup> Singaporean Mandarin is based on simplified Chinese and it is similar to the system used in mainland China. The forms of Mandarin spoken in Singapore range from <a href="/wiki/Standard_Mandarin" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard Mandarin">Standard Mandarin</a> to a pidgin known as <a href="/w/index.php?title=Singdarin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Singdarin (not yet started)">Singdarin</a>. Besides <a href="/w/index.php?title=Singaporean_Mandarin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Singaporean Mandarin (not yet started)">Mandarin</a>, many southern Chinese dialects are also spoken in Singapore. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Hokkien" title="Hokkien">Hokkien</a> used to be a <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a> among the Singaporean Chinese so many older Singaporeans still understand <a href="/wiki/Hokkien" title="Hokkien">Hokkien</a>. The most common Chinese dialects spoken by Singaporeans are the <a href="/wiki/Hokkien" title="Hokkien">Hokkien</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hainan" title="Hainan">Hainan</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Teochew&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Teochew (not yet started)">Teochew</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cantonese_language" title="Cantonese language">Cantonese</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-country-data.com_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-country-data.com-58">[56]</a></sup> However, Chinese dialects other than Mandarin are not allowed in the media, so these dialects are quickly dying out. Most younger Singaporeans do not speak them anymore. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">Tamil</a> is spoken by about 60% of Indians in Singapore. That is about 5% of all Singaporeans. Indian languages such as <a href="/wiki/Malayalam" title="Malayalam">Malayalam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Telugu_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Telugu language">Telugu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a> are also spoken by a small group of Singaporean Indians in Singapore. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=12" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Culture">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Change section: Culture">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Singapore has many kinds of people and immigrants from many places. Therefore, Singaporean culture has often been described as a mix of cultures – British, Malay, Chinese, Indian and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Peranakan&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Peranakan (not yet started)">Peranakan</a>. Also, foreigners are 42% of the population in Singapore<sup id="cite_ref-un.org_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-un.org-52">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-singstat.gov.sg_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-singstat.gov.sg-60">[58]</a></sup> and they are part of changing Singaporean culture. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food">Food</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=13" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Food">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Change section: Food">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Hainanese_Chicken_Rice.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Hainanese_Chicken_Rice.jpg/200px-Hainanese_Chicken_Rice.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="125" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Hainanese_Chicken_Rice.jpg/300px-Hainanese_Chicken_Rice.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Hainanese_Chicken_Rice.jpg/400px-Hainanese_Chicken_Rice.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="624"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Hainanese_Chicken_Rice.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Hainanese chicken rice, a local food in Singapore
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Dining is an important part of life in Singapore.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[59]</a></sup> Singaporean food is an example of the many different cultures in the country. It is also an example of mixing among cultures. British, Chinese, Indian, Malay, Tamil, and Indonesian styles of cooking all mix together. It is especially known for its sea food. Typical Singaporean food includes: <a href="/wiki/Satay" title="Satay">Satay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nasi_lemak" title="Nasi lemak">Nasi lemak</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Chilli_crab&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Chilli crab (not yet started)">Chilli crab</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hainanese_chicken_rice" title="Hainanese chicken rice">Hainanese chicken rice</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=14" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Media">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Change section: Media">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/MediaCorp" class="mw-redirect" title="MediaCorp">MediaCorp</a>, the state-owned media corporation, operates all seven local broadcast television channels in Singapore. It also runs 13 radio stations of the total 18 radio stations in Singapore.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[60]</a></sup> Radio and television stations are all owned by government controlled companies. However, one radio transmitter in Singapore is not controlled by the government. That is the Far Eastern Relay Station of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC_World_Service&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="BBC World Service (not yet started)">BBC World Service</a>. </p>
      <p>Print media of Singapore includes 16 newspapers and several magazines. Daily newspapers are published in English, <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Mandarin language">Chinese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malay_language" title="Malay language">Malay</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">Tamil</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="National_flower">National flower</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=15" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: National flower">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Change section: National flower">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:VandaMissJoaquim.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/VandaMissJoaquim.jpg/200px-VandaMissJoaquim.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/VandaMissJoaquim.jpg/300px-VandaMissJoaquim.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/VandaMissJoaquim.jpg/400px-VandaMissJoaquim.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:VandaMissJoaquim.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The national flower of Singapore
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The national flower of Singapore is Vanda Miss Joaquim. It is a type of <a href="/wiki/Orchid" title="Orchid">orchid</a> and it is a hybrid orchid. This makes Singapore the only nation in the world to have a <a href="/wiki/Hybrid" title="Hybrid">hybrid</a> as a national flower. It was chosen because it was part of the effort to create national pride and identity.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[61]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=16" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Economy">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Change section: Economy">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Singapore has a strong and free economy that supports a large middle class. The city state is a global <a href="/wiki/Shipping" class="mw-redirect" title="Shipping">shipping</a> and <a href="/wiki/Logistics" title="Logistics">logistics</a> hub and many multinational firms have their offices in Singapore. The national airline, <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Airlines" title="Singapore Airlines">Singapore Airlines</a> has a large global network which brings tourists and business travelers alike, to the city. </p>
      <p>Singapore also has a port located at the south of Singapore, called Keppel Harbour. It is one of the busiest ports around the world with many ships coming in to trade in a single day.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[62]</a></sup> Singapore also has another port on <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jurong_Island&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jurong Island (not yet started)">Jurong Island</a>. </p> 
      <div class="center">
       <div class="thumb tnone">
        <div class="thumbinner" style="width:802px;">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Singapore_port_panorama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Singapore_port_panorama.jpg/800px-Singapore_port_panorama.jpg" decoding="async" width="800" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Singapore_port_panorama.jpg/1200px-Singapore_port_panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Singapore_port_panorama.jpg/1600px-Singapore_port_panorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="10000" data-file-height="1842"></a> 
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          <div class="magnify">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Singapore_port_panorama.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
          </div>The port of Singapore is one of the busiest ports in the world.
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Money">Money</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=17" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Money">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Change section: Money">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Singapore_dollar" title="Singapore dollar">Singapore dollar</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Singapore's <a href="/wiki/Currency" title="Currency">currency</a> is the Singapore <a href="/wiki/Dollar" title="Dollar">dollar</a>. The short name for the <a href="/wiki/Singapore_dollar" title="Singapore dollar">Singapore dollar</a> is SGD. <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a> dollar can be used in Singapore, because they have the same <a href="/wiki/Value" title="Value">value</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[63]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of January 2018, one US dollar is about $1.35 Singapore dollars. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=18" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Geography">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Change section: Geography">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:CIA_World_Factbook_map_of_Singapore_(English).png" class="image"><img alt="Map showing Singapore's island and the territories belonging Singapore and its neighbours" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/CIA_World_Factbook_map_of_Singapore_%28English%29.png/220px-CIA_World_Factbook_map_of_Singapore_%28English%29.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/07/CIA_World_Factbook_map_of_Singapore_%28English%29.png 1.5x" data-file-width="327" data-file-height="350"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:CIA_World_Factbook_map_of_Singapore_(English).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A Map of Singapore and the surrounding islands &amp; waterways
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Singapore is made up of 63 islands, including the main island, which is known as Singapore Island to most people, but is also known as Pulau Ujong.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[64]</a></sup> There are two man-made connections to <a href="/wiki/Johor" title="Johor">Johor</a>, Malaysia: the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Johor%E2%80%93Singapore_Causeway&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Johor–Singapore Causeway (not yet started)">Johor–Singapore Causeway</a> in the north, and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Malaysia%E2%80%93Singapore_Second_Link&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Malaysia–Singapore Second Link (not yet started)">Tuas Second Link</a> in the west. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jurong_Island&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jurong Island (not yet started)">Jurong Island</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pulau_Tekong&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Pulau Tekong (not yet started)">Pulau Tekong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pulau_Ubin" title="Pulau Ubin">Pulau Ubin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sentosa" title="Sentosa">Sentosa</a> are the largest of Singapore's smaller islands. The highest natural point is <a href="/wiki/Bukit_Timah" title="Bukit Timah">Bukit Timah Hill</a> at 166&nbsp;m (545&nbsp;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[65]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>About 23% of Singapore's land area are forest and nature reserves.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[66]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Urbanisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Urbanisation">Urbanisation</a> has removed most primary <a href="/wiki/Rainforest" title="Rainforest">rainforest</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Bukit_Timah_Nature_Reserve" title="Bukit Timah Nature Reserve">Bukit Timah Nature Reserve</a> the only significant remaining forest.<sup id="cite_ref-earthshots.usgs.gov_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earthshots.usgs.gov-69">[67]</a></sup> Even though there is very little primary rainforest left, there are more than 300 parks and four nature reserves in Singapore. There are also many trees planted all over Singapore and almost fifty per cent of the country is covered by trees and plants. Because of this, Singapore is also commonly known as the 'Garden City'.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[68]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Singapore, being a small country, has been reclaiming land from the sea around the island. The first time Singapore started to reclaim land was in the 1960s. The total land area of Singapore at that time was 581.5&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> and it has increased to 633&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> in the 1990s, which is an increase of about 9% in total land area.<sup id="cite_ref-thinkquest_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thinkquest-71">[69]</a></sup> It is now 704&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (272&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), and may grow by another 100&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (40&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) by 2030.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[70]</a></sup> Some land reclamation projects involve joining together smaller islands to make larger islands with more uses, like Jurong Island.<sup id="cite_ref-earthshots.usgs.gov_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earthshots.usgs.gov-69">[67]</a></sup> Singapore uses the <a href="/wiki/Land_reclamation#Landfill" title="Land reclamation">landfill</a> method to reclaim the sea at the south of the country. The country's rapid reclamation projects has made disputes with its neighbouring countries, Malaysia and Indonesia.<sup id="cite_ref-Singapore_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Singapore-73">[71]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=19" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Climate">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Change section: Climate">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Symphony_Lake,_Singapore_Botanic_Gardens_-_20041025.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Symphony_Lake%2C_Singapore_Botanic_Gardens_-_20041025.jpg/200px-Symphony_Lake%2C_Singapore_Botanic_Gardens_-_20041025.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Symphony_Lake%2C_Singapore_Botanic_Gardens_-_20041025.jpg/300px-Symphony_Lake%2C_Singapore_Botanic_Gardens_-_20041025.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Symphony_Lake%2C_Singapore_Botanic_Gardens_-_20041025.jpg/400px-Symphony_Lake%2C_Singapore_Botanic_Gardens_-_20041025.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1296" data-file-height="972"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Symphony_Lake,_Singapore_Botanic_Gardens_-_20041025.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Singapore botanic garden, which is part of Singapore's forests.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Singapore is <a href="/wiki/Hot" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot">hot</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wet" class="mw-redirect" title="Wet">wet</a> all year round. It has a tropical <a href="/wiki/Rainforest" title="Rainforest">rainforest</a> climate (<i>Af</i> in the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>), which means there are no <a href="/wiki/Seasons" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Seasons">seasons</a> (<a href="/wiki/Spring" title="Spring">spring</a>, <a href="/wiki/Summer" title="Summer">summer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Autumn" title="Autumn">autumn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Winter" title="Winter">winter</a>) in Singapore. There is the most <a href="/wiki/Rain" title="Rain">rain</a> at the end of the year, and the <a href="/wiki/Temperature" title="Temperature">temperature</a> is usually around 20&nbsp;°C to 35&nbsp;°C.<sup id="cite_ref-weather_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-weather-74">[72]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-weather2_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-weather2-75">[73]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Although Singapore does not experience the four seasons, the period from May to June is usually warmer, while the period from November to January is cooler because of the more frequent rains and monsoonal winds in Singapore during the year-end.<sup id="cite_ref-weather_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-weather-74">[72]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-weather2_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-weather2-75">[73]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Relations_with_other_countries">Relations with other countries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=20" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Relations with other countries">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Change section: Relations with other countries">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Singapore has <a href="/wiki/Diplomacy" title="Diplomacy">diplomatic relations</a> with 175 other Sovereign states.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[76]</a></sup> Singapore's <a href="/wiki/Foreign_policy" title="Foreign policy">foreign policy</a> is to maintain a secure environment in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a> as well as the countries near Southeast Asia. A basic rule is the political and economic stability in Southeast Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[77]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="ASEAN">ASEAN</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=21" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: ASEAN">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Change section: ASEAN">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Singapore is part of the <a href="/wiki/ASEAN" class="mw-redirect" title="ASEAN">ASEAN</a> (Association of the South East Asian nations) network, which is an organisation that unites all Southeast Asian countries. Member countries of ASEAN work with and help other countries in ASEAN. Singapore is one of the countries that founded ASEAN.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[78]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Commonwealth_of_Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=22" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Commonwealth of Nations">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Change section: Commonwealth of Nations">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Singapore is also part of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>, which is for countries that used to be under the British.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[79]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Land_reclamation">Land reclamation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=23" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Land reclamation">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Change section: Land reclamation">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Singapore, being a small country, has been reclaiming land from the sea around the island. The first time Singapore started to reclaim land was in the 1960s. The total land area of Singapore at that time was 581.5&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> and it has increased to 633&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> in the 1990s, which is an increase of about 9% in total land area.<sup id="cite_ref-thinkquest_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thinkquest-71">[69]</a></sup> Singapore uses the <a href="/wiki/Land_reclamation#Landfill" title="Land reclamation">landfill</a> method to reclaim the sea at the south of the country. The country's rapid reclamation projects has made disputes with its neighbouring countries, Malaysia and Indonesia.<sup id="cite_ref-Singapore_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Singapore-73">[71]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Singapore reclaims lots of land due to the following reasons:<sup id="cite_ref-thinkquest_71-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thinkquest-71">[69]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>The small size of the country.</li> 
       <li>There is a rising demand for more land as the population increases.</li>
      </ul> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Holidays">Holidays</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=24" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Holidays">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Change section: Holidays">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:CIA_World_Factbook_map_of_Singapore_(English).gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/CIA_World_Factbook_map_of_Singapore_%28English%29.gif/200px-CIA_World_Factbook_map_of_Singapore_%28English%29.gif" decoding="async" width="200" height="214" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/CIA_World_Factbook_map_of_Singapore_%28English%29.gif/300px-CIA_World_Factbook_map_of_Singapore_%28English%29.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c2/CIA_World_Factbook_map_of_Singapore_%28English%29.gif 2x" data-file-width="329" data-file-height="352"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:CIA_World_Factbook_map_of_Singapore_(English).gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map of Singapore
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Public holidays in Singapore:<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[80]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/New_Year" title="New Year">New Year</a>'s Day</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Chinese_New_Year" title="Chinese New Year">Chinese New Year</a> (<a href="/wiki/Chinese_people" title="Chinese people">Chinese</a> <a href="/wiki/Festival" title="Festival">Festival</a>) – 2 days</li> 
       <li>Good Friday</li> 
       <li>Labour Day</li> 
       <li>Vesak Day (<a href="/wiki/Buddhist" class="mw-redirect" title="Buddhist">Buddhist</a> <a href="/wiki/Festival" title="Festival">Festival</a>)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/National_Day" title="National Day">National Day</a></li> 
       <li>Hari Raya Puasa (<a href="/wiki/Malays" title="Malays">Malay</a> <a href="/wiki/Festival" title="Festival">Festival</a>)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Deepavali" class="mw-redirect" title="Deepavali">Deepavali</a> (<a href="/wiki/India" title="India">Indian</a> <a href="/wiki/Festival" title="Festival">Festival</a>)</li> 
       <li>Hari Raya Haji (<a href="/wiki/Malays" title="Malays">Malay</a> <a href="/wiki/Festival" title="Festival">Festival</a>)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Christmas" title="Christmas">Christmas</a> Day</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>There are also <a href="/wiki/School" title="School">school</a> holidays, lasting one week in <a href="/wiki/March" title="March">March</a> and <a href="/wiki/September" title="September">September</a>, about one month in <a href="/wiki/June" title="June">June</a>, and about one and a half months in <a href="/wiki/December" title="December">December</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[81]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Records">Records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=25" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Records">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Change section: Records">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sg-flyer-4oct07.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Sg-flyer-4oct07.jpg/200px-Sg-flyer-4oct07.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Sg-flyer-4oct07.jpg/300px-Sg-flyer-4oct07.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Sg-flyer-4oct07.jpg/400px-Sg-flyer-4oct07.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sg-flyer-4oct07.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Singapore Flyer
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Singapore holds records with its buildings and people. Some are: </p> 
      <table class="wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Type of record</th> 
         <th>Name of record</th> 
         <th>Received record </th>
        </tr>

         <td>Building</td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Singapore_Flyer" title="Singapore Flyer">Singapore Flyer</a></td> 
         <td>For the tallest Ferris wheel in the world<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[82]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table>
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=26" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Transportation">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Change section: Transportation">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:KUB-EuroV-SBST.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/KUB-EuroV-SBST.JPG/200px-KUB-EuroV-SBST.JPG" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/KUB-EuroV-SBST.JPG/300px-KUB-EuroV-SBST.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/KUB-EuroV-SBST.JPG/400px-KUB-EuroV-SBST.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:KUB-EuroV-SBST.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Buses can take riders to almost any part of Singapore, even those not reached by MRTs
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>There are <a href="/wiki/Bus" title="Bus">buses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Railway">trains</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Taxi" title="Taxi">taxis</a> in Singapore. </p>
      <p>Singapore has a <a href="/wiki/Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Railway">railway</a> system known as the <a href="/wiki/Mass_Rapid_Transit_(Singapore)" title="Mass Rapid Transit (Singapore)">Mass Rapid Transit</a>, or MRT in short. There are also <a href="/wiki/Taxi" title="Taxi">taxi</a> companies like Comfort Cabs, Silver Cab, SMRT Taxis, CityCab and Premier Taxi.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[83]</a></sup> There is one telephone number to call a taxi, of which the closest taxi from any company will respond.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[84]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Mass Rapid Transit of Singapore is the most commonly used form of transportation in Singapore.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[85]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[86]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Singaporean land transport system is controlled by the LTA (Land Transport Authority) of Singapore.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[87]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airport">Airport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=27" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Airport">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Singapore&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Change section: Airport">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Changi_Airport" title="Singapore Changi Airport">Singapore Changi Airport</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Aerial_view_of_Singapore_Changi_Airport_and_Changi_Air_Base_-_20110523.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Aerial_view_of_Singapore_Changi_Airport_and_Changi_Air_Base_-_20110523.jpg/300px-Aerial_view_of_Singapore_Changi_Airport_and_Changi_Air_Base_-_20110523.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Aerial_view_of_Singapore_Changi_Airport_and_Changi_Air_Base_-_20110523.jpg/450px-Aerial_view_of_Singapore_Changi_Airport_and_Changi_Air_Base_-_20110523.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Aerial_view_of_Singapore_Changi_Airport_and_Changi_Air_Base_-_20110523.jpg/600px-Aerial_view_of_Singapore_Changi_Airport_and_Changi_Air_Base_-_20110523.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2616" data-file-height="1742"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Aerial_view_of_Singapore_Changi_Airport_and_Changi_Air_Base_-_20110523.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>An aerial view of Changi International Airport.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Singapore Changi Airport is the main airport of Singapore. It is in the east of Singapore, with a total of four terminals with airlines flying to many different parts of the world. It has also received many awards for being the best airport in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CHANGI_NLB-SG_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CHANGI_NLB-SG-91">[89]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The airport is in <a href="/wiki/Changi" title="Changi">Changi</a>. It is on a 13 square kilometres (5.0 sq mi) site which was <a href="#Land_reclamation">reclaimed</a> from the sea.<sup id="cite_ref-CHANGI_NLB-SG_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CHANGI_NLB-SG-91">[89]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div>

Usually thought of <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> for <a href="/wiki/Culture" title="Culture">cultural</a>, <a href="/wiki/Politics" title="Politics">political</a> and <a href="/wiki/History" title="History">historical</a> reasons. 3. Special territories. 4. Disputed territories.</small>
